I INTRODUCTION
The city of Jinzhou is the center of economv, culture and transportation in the west
part of Liaoning Province. WVitlh economv growth and the rising standards of living, the
demand for water supply in the city increases dramnatically and the available water supply
system is f?r from being able to meet the requirements. On account of pollution sources
and the polluted Xiaoling River, ground water at shallow depths in the urban areas is gen-
erally polluted, intensifying the lack of water supplies in the city, and seriously hindering
the developmnent of economy and the raising of living standards in Jinzhou. In order to
solve this problem, the Ji.nzhou People's Government has decided to construct a new water
supply from liuduan to Baduan on the right hand side bank of the Daling River, where
large quantities of good quality water are available. To further ensure the maintenance of
the good quality of the water in that area, the government has also decided to curb the
pollution caused by the sewage of the Jincheng Paper Mill, Which is located in the upper
reaches of the water supply river.
The two above- mentioned projects are the sub- projects of the No. 2 World Bank
Loan Project for urban reconstruction programme of cities in Liaoning province. Based on
the document reference (86) NE 003 and the relevant requirements of WB, and entrust-
ed by tl.-: Office for City Reconstruction Programnme of Jinzhou Municipality, Chinese
Research Academy of Environmental Sciences undertook the task of compiling an EIA
re port for the two projects.
Since the two projects are closely related to each other, a unified EIA report is sensi-
ble. However, the unique features of each project are described separately in the
report.

3 OBJECITVE OF ETA AND TARGET FOR ENVTRONMENT
PROTECTION
3. 1 Objective of EIA
Forecast and analysis will be made of the iTnpact on the enviromnent of Jinzhou city
and around the project sites as caused by the construction of the new water supply and the
curbing of the pollution by sewage from Jincheng Paper Mill. A feasibility study will be
made for site selection, technology used and measures to curb pollution for the two pro-
jects. Suggestions will be made regarding further improvement and protection of environ-
ment and scientific basis will be provided for decision-making organizations.
3. 2 Target for Environment Protection
Basnd on the objectives of the two construction project and the geographic locations
of sites, the major subjects for environment protection are ground water resources and
surface water resources.
3. 2. 1 Target for Curbing Pollution Sources
In order to prevent the quality of the water in Daling River and the ground water in
the lower reaches of the river from being poUuted, it is necessary tQ put under control the
3
recycied paper                                          evologv nd emrnmnt



i
quantity of polluutants discharged from the major pollution sources along the Daling River.
The majot polluting source in the lower reaches of Dating River is Jincheng Paper Mill. It
is therefore required that the discharge quantity of COD shall not exceed 61 tfd, of SS
48t/d after 1995 and that by 2000 the disclarge of CODcoshould-be less than 7t/d.
3. 2. 2 Target for Water Quality of Daling River
Daling River serves as a flood-relief channel, water supply for both agriculture and
industry, and a complementary water supply for ground water in the river sector area.
The near-term target (1995) for water quality is that the quality of water in river sec-
tions below the Jincheng Paper Mill shall be improved significantly. The mid-term target
(2000) is that the water quality should be further improved to the extent that the soluble
COD1, CODc, should reach Class III standard in river sections below the Paper Mill and
that the quality of water penetrating into the complementary sector should reach Grade 2
requirement for water supply protection. The long-term target is that water quality in riv-
er sections below the Paper Mill should reach standard Clas m, GB 3838-88, enabling
Daing River to supplement gtound water sources and remain in good ecological sea envi-
ronment conditions.
4  OVERVIEW OF ENVIRONMENT IN CONSTRUCnION
AREA
4. 1 Natural Environment
4. 1. 1 Geogtrphic Location
Te city of Jinzhou is situated in the west part of Liaoning provice, east longitude
120"42'-122"37', north latitude 40°48'-42-07', borderd in the east with Shenyang
and Panjing and in the north with Fuxin and Jinxi, and in the south with the Liaodong
Bay of the Bohai Sea. Downtown Jinzhou is situated at east longitude 121'08', north
latidude 41-08' with an area of 10,300km2. Jincheng Paper Mill is located at Jincheng
Town, 25 km to the northeast of the urban area on the left side of Daling River, i. e.,
eat longitude 121'20'1 north latidude 41110'. The geological survey area for the new
4



water supply project is delimited by E 121'13'1 '-- 121'28'18", N .Ps'O!' 3P'?--
41"10'00". See Fig. 1 - 3 for geographic locations of Jinzhou and the sites for the two
projects.
4. 1. 2 Wcather and Climate
Jinzhou features a north temperate zone, semi-humid, trade wind type, continental e-
climate. The main characteristics of its climate are cold winter, hot summer, distinction
among the four seasons, big difference in temperature between day and night, and un-
even rainfall. Average yearly temperature is 9..I1C, with max temperature of. 37. 3tC
and min of minus 24. 7C.
Jinzhou's spring features strong wind and rare rain, quick warming, large quantity
of evaporation of water, and susceptibiLity to draugt. In mid-March, soil starts to thaw
and in nmid April most areas no longer have frost. The spring sees the highest wind speed
of the vear, the average speed being 5m/s, in May wind speed decreases. Summer has
high temperature and much rain, the average temperature being 20 C from June to Au-
gust, the average temperature of July, the hottest month of the year, over 241C. In
June 1972 Jinzhou experienced its highest ever temperature, 41. 8g. The average air
huniidity of July and August reaches 80%, the highest of the year. Rainfal in summer
is 360- 430mm, constituting over two thirds of the total rainfall of the year. Rainfall is
the greatest in July, 150-200mm on the average. Autumn is warm and scarce of rain
with sunny days. Temperature drops sharply in this season. The average temperature in
September is around 18C, but by the end of the month there will be frost. The rainfall
of this season is 80-120mm, only 15% to 19% of the total amount of the year. Au-
tumn enjoys abundant sunshine but daily sharp drop in temperature. Winter feature dry
and cold weather with very little rain and snow. The day is very often fine although bit-
ter cold and dry. January is the coldest month with an average temperature of -9 to
-11 C. The lowest temperatures ever reached were between -25 and - 291C. Rain and
snow-fall is about 20mm, only 3 %-4 % of the total amount of the year. The average
yearly rainfall is 573. 9mm approximately with that of July and August being 60 %. The
average water evaporation is 1, 827. 2mm. The principal wind direction over the year is
south south west. The average depth of frozen soil in the past years is 1. 2m.
5
recycled paper                                          eology and envirnment



4. 1. 3 Topography
Generally speaking, the city of Jinzhou lies in an area which slopes from northwest
to southeast. The urban areas are surrounded in south, east and north by hills. The city
is 20-70m above sea level. To the northwest borders of the sector areas of Daling River
and Xiaoling River, are hills whose absolute height is 20-lOOm. The hinterland of these
sectors are alluvial plains, tilting from northweat to southeast at a slope of 0. 9%0 with an
absolute height of 10-24m. The coastal area features solonchak soil and marshes.
4. 1. 4 Surface Water System
Daling and Xiaoling Rivers are the two mnajor rivers running through the area under
environment impact assesment.
Rising in Yaolugou, Jianchang, Daling River runs through Chaoyang, Beipiao,
Yixian County, and Jinxian County, covering a distance of 403kn, before it enters the
Bohai Sea. The area of the reaches upwards from the hydrological station of Jinxian
County amounts 23, 048km2. The annual flow of the Daling River was 1.540 million m2
between 1961 and 1987. The river contains much sand, the average sand content being
13. 8kg/m3and the highest content 90. 3kg/m3. With large quantities of organic Materials
washed into the river from the soil on the banks and the discharge of sewage from both in-
dustry (especially from the Jincheng Paper Mill) and living quarters, Dalng River suf-
fers from severe pollution, and its water quality falls short of the GB 3838-88V stan-
dards.
The 206 km long Xiaoling River rises from the Kala mountain at Chaoyang. It has
two branches; Nuer River and Baiyigu River, which are 136 km and 30 km long respec-
tively. The total area of their reaches is 5, 480km2, of which 4,444. 6km2 lies in the re-
gion in question. After passing through the Taihe District of Jinzhou and Niangniang
Place Town of Jinxian County, Xiaoling River runs into the Bohai Sea. The average
flow of the river per year is 330 million mlbetween 1961 and 1987. On account of the
discharge of sewage from the industrial and residential areas of the city, Xiaoliang River
is severely polluted and its water quality falls short of GB3838-88V standards. See Fag.
4 for the distribution of surface water systems of Jinzhou.
4.1.5  Geological Environment
6



The EL area lies in weat slopes in the concave reaches of the Lower Liao River,
where, since Cainozoic, the earth crust sank and the deposits fromed the tertiary system
of stratum. Beneath this stratum is granite of the Yanshan Period and atratum o" the
Great Wall ststem of the Early Proterozoic period.
The Pre- fourth Period stratum  Its nain contents are conglomerate quartz- and
manganese powder-containing sandstone, shale and limestone. They are found mainly in
the western hilly land of the EIA area.
The granite of the Yanshan period is intrusion rock-cropping up in the northern hilly
land.
The early tertiary system stratum of the Cenozoic era: The cornposition revealed by
drilling is grey sandstone, conglomerate, multi- colour sandstone, mudstone featured by
poor adhesiveness. This stratum is mainly found underneath the plain in the southeast.
The Fourth Period stratum: This stratum in the EIA area is relatively mature with a
thickness of up to 10 to 80 meters. A detailed description of the geological features of this
stratum is given below.
1) The mid-Pleistocene (Q2) slope diluvium: found mainly in slopes and valleys of
the hilly land. Its main contents are brown red and brown yellow sub-clay and sand
mixed gravel. Generally, its thickness is less than lOm. The alluviation is found in the
plain comprising brown subclay in the upper layer and gravel, pebble and sand in the
lower part with a thickness of 10 to 30m.
2) The early Pleistocene (Q3)  Slope diluvium is found in hilly land consisting of
brown powder-like subsand, subclay, and thin layers of sand and gravel. The thickness
is normally less than 10 meters. The alluviatiaion is distributed in the plain comprising
brown clay in the upper layer and sand gravel in the lower layer with a thickness of 20 to
40 m.
3) The Holocene(Q4): It is scattered in the surface of the plain with alluviation as
main content. It comprises subsand, fine sand, and grey muddy subsand and subclay in
the base with a thickness less than 10 m.
4. 1. 6   Hydrologic and Geologic Environment
The ground water in the EIA area exists mainly in the water-containing layer of
sand, gravel and pebble of the fourth svstem. The ground water features relatively stable
recycled paper                                          ecolog and mnvim nmcni
7



distribution, abundant quantity and excellent quality. The thickness increases gradually
from northwest to southeast, the structure transforms from a single layer to a double lay-
er, and the hydraulic nature from underground current to pressurized water. Thbe under-
ground stream runs from northeast to southwest on the west bank of the Daling River,
and from northwest to southeast on the east bank of Daling River. Water-containing lay-
ers in the ETA area can be divided into three categories in terms of their characteristics and
hydraulic nature.
Single layer underground current-light pressurized water containing layer: Such a
layer usually is covered by a 3 to 1Om thick clay. Only in the river bed of Daling River
beyond Liuduan and in the ancient river beds can one find such water layers without clay
covering. The water layer is composed of gravel and pebble of early and nid Pleistocene
with a thickness of 20 to 50m and the maximum thickness of up to 60m. The groudwater
table is 3 to 5m deep and in Liuduan 5 to 8m deep. The ground here has a good Perme-
ability with a permeability coefficient of 150 to 250m/d, an influence radius of 300 to
500m. A single well can produce 5, 000 tons of water per day or even more than that. In
Liuduan, daily output reaches 10,000 to 20,000 t per day. The water is of gooa quali-
ty, being low mineralized, heavy calsium carbonate or calsium magnesium carbonate
tvpe water with mineralization less than 0. 5g/1.
Double layer pressurized water at shaUow and great depths: These layers are dis-
tributed mainly in the southeast part of the ETA area. The shallow water layers are topped
with a 10 to 25 m thick layer of clay. The water containing layer comprises pebble,
gravel and sand with a thickness of 20 to 30 m and permeability coefficient of 100 to 150
mn per day. A single well produces 5,000 to 10,000 tons of water per day.
The underlying layers carry pressurized water and the water separating layer is atS to
10 m layer of clay and subclay at a depth of 40 to 50 meters. The water-containing lay-
ers are formed by gravels and pebbles 20 to 40 meters in thickness with an osmotic roeffi-
cicnt of 5 to 4 0 m/d. Normally a single -vell can produce 1, 000 to 3,000 tons of water
per day.
In the hillv area, the crevices of the bed rock contains karst water and the slope dilu-
vial laycrs have small voids. The water containing-layers are buried at great depths and
are not stable, or water-rich. They are lateral feed sources for water containing layers in
the EIA area.
8



The principal feeding sources for groundwater in the EIA area are infiltration of
rivers, precipitation and permeability while the secondary sources are lateral run-off and
back infiltration from irrigation. The groundwater table is 9 to 12 meters. and flouws to
south, southeast.
The hydraulic slope is 0. 5%4-1. 2%.The drain of ground water is mnainly by me-
chanical vertical extraction and secondarily by horizontal flow discharge. Dynamic
changes win be controUed bv climate and rmnual extraction.
4:1. 7 Maritime Environment
The sea areas of Jinzhou are situated at the top of the Liaodong Bay, beginning at
the estuary of Daling River (Erdaohc in Jinxian County and ending at the mouth of Lao-
he River in Tianqiao Town with a coastline of 94. 2km.
The sea areas of Jinzhou feature high altitutes, shallow waters with low transparen-
cy. The lowest water temperature in winter is minus 2 deg c and the highest water tem-
perature in summer is 27 deg c. In spring, water temperature rises and there is a signifi-
cant temperature difference. The avcrage water temperatute over the year is 15. 7 deg c.
In early December waters along thc coast begin to freeze and start to melt in March next
ycar. The average salinity is 29. 7 % , which is significantly influenced by heat radiation
from the continent.
Liaodong Bay has complex motion of tides, which are different from north to south.
irregular half-day tide occurs in the north from Daling River and Xiaoling River to
Ciangshansi of Xingcheng, and high tide height difference is 1. 5 m; the southern part of
the Bay is from Changsbansi of Xingcheng to Tianlongsi of Suizhong. Basically speaking,
tide current in Liaodong Bay flows along the coast to the northeaset and southwest. Near
Hulu Iland, the high tide flows towards the northeast and the .ebb flows to southwest
Near Xinlitun in the sector land of Daling River and Xiaoling River, the high tide goes
northeast and the ebb southwest. The speed of the flow is 1. 2 knots (0. 62 mWs).
The biological features of the sea areas of Jinzhou are not distinct. The sea water is
fertile enough for marine life to lay eggs. grow and live. In the sea area there are 30
genera of phytoplankton. The community structure is the diatom genus. Superior species
include chain algae, round algae, bone algae. There are 16 categories of zooplanktons
which may be subdivided into 51 species. Superior species include flexible foot. strong
9
recycled paper                                           cology and envirn,nir,wu



arrowworm and nociluCa. Bigger zooplankt3ns are rhopilema esoulents and stomopholus
nomurai.
Demersal life in off-shore areas of Jinzhou (sea waters within isobath of 10m) is
mainly echinoderms moUuses and arthrupods. In the sector sea areas near Dating and Xi-
aoling Rivers live several kinds of clans.
Swimnuing. life in liaodong Bay includes (according to survey made between 1983
and 1984) 106 species of fish, 3 speces of prawns and 2 species of cephalopod. Major
speies of fish are small yellow croakerns, hair-tails, blue-spot threadfins, rays, yeUow
crucian carp and perches Prawns include Chinese prawns, mantis shrimps and white
prawns. Cephalopad includes cuttlefish.
4.1. 8 Vegeation Environment
Jinzhou lies in a narrow strip of land, which in terms of vegetation, falls into the
pan-arctic vegetation zone, the sub-zone of Sino-Japan forest plants, north China re-
gion, north China plain and sub-mountainous zone. As there is a distinct difference in
temperature between north and south, a significant diference in rainfall over the year and
a variety of topography, there exist a great number of vegeuation forms in the area of
Jinzhou. In te northwest hill areas there are tree major formns of vegetation; coniferous
trues, broadleaf trees, bushes and -grass. The southeast coast features pasLure and marsh
vegetations. The site of the two project salt and alkali psure land. In the lower reaches
of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers, where there are narshes and land covered with water,
marsh and water vegetation prevails. Marsh vegcetion includes reads and fragrant catta
and water vegetation includes duckweods and lotus
4. 2 Social Environment
4. 2.1  A _dsuatve Dlstricts and Popudation
Jinzhou has jurisdiction over 4 districts and 4 counties with a population of 2. 93
million.
iTh urban area of Jinzhou is 10 kan from east to west and 7 km from north to south
and amounts to an area of 67km2, of which built-up area is 45km2. 'Tbe population of
the urban area is 0. 74 million, including 569,000 persons who are not engaged in agri-
10



culture.
Jincheng Town is under the jurisdiction of Jinxian County. The town has a built-up
area of 2km2 with a population of 22,000.
Opposite to Jincheng Town is Daling River Town, the seat of the County Govern-
ment of Jinxian. Daling River Town has a built-up area of 6kcm2 and a population of
30, 000.
Near the pressure station, the water distribution station and along the water supply
pipes are 9 villages with 910 households totaling 3,640 persons.
4. 2. 2 Social and Economic Status
Jinzhou is a coastal industrial city with powerful industrial infrastructure and a com-
plete range of trades. Its main industries include petro-chernics, netallurgy and nachine-
building, textile, paper naking, electric power, building material, medicine and elec-
tronics. In 1990, the total output value of industry was 8. 7 billion yuan RMB.
The only industry in lincheng Town is paper nmaking besides service industries.
However, Daling River Town has a number of enterprise engaged ir, paper mnaking, pro-
duction of chemical fertilizer and machine building.
Jinzhou also boasts a prosperous agriculture, anu is an important producer of grain,
vegetable oil, cash crops, fruit, and aquatic product in Liaoning province. There are al-
together 360, 000 hectares of arable land. Major crops are corn, gaoliang, soy beans,
cotton, peanuts, and rice. In 1990, the total output value of agriculture was 2. 4 billion
yuan-RMB.
The EIA area in the sectors of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers is about 831km2. Major
crops are corn, gaoliang, rice. In the coastal area in the south, there are 4,700 hectares
of artificially-bred prawn ponds!
Jinzhou is the hub of transportation linking northeast China and north China. There
are well built networks of railways, highways, ports and airports. Eight railways meet at
Jinzhou. The port of Jinzhou is Class 1 port for overseas trade with berths for ten thou-
sand ton and upwards bulk cargo ships, crude oil tankers, and finished product tankers.
The airport of Jinzhou is fit for operation of medium-sized aircraft. [DD service is avail-
able, enabling communication with over 182 cities abroad. The economic development
zone of Jinzhou port and the hi-tech development zone south of the Xiaoling River in the
11

urban area comprise flat land with easy transportation and enjoy proferential policies.
They have already become a window opening to the outside world.
Jinzhou has developed its infrastructure at fast speeds. At present there are seven
waterworks all using groundwater and producing 266, 500 tons of water per day, of
which 6 tons are supplied to Jinxi every day. In the urban area the total length of water-
pipes is 762 km. Every household uses tap water. The average water consumption is 162
litres per person per day in urban areas. For each output value of 10,000 yuan, 359 tons
of water are consumed. The total length of sewage pipes is 211. 3 km, benefiting 75%
households. No sewage treatment facilities are available. Sewage from living quarters and
factories is all discharged into Xiaoling River. Daily discharge is 220, 000 tons. The bulk.
of the sewage of Jincheng Town and Dalinghe Town (5, DOOt/d) is discharged into the ir-
rigation ditches of Daling River. The sewage of Jinxian Chemical Fertilizer Factory and
the Paper Mill (24, OOOt|d) is discharged into Daling River.
5 ENGINEERING ANALYSIS OF THE CONSTRUCITON PRO-
JECI
5. 1 Nature of the Construction Project
5. 1. 1 Nature of the Project for Constructing a New Waterworks for Jinzhou
At present there are 7 waterworks at Jinzhou. The Bozi and Suifeng waterworks are
located in the alluvial sectors of Daling River and Xiaoling River respecuvely. The water
sources for the remaining 5 waterworks are rivers being supplied by sballow groundwater.
llmc total water supply capacity of the municipality is 265,600 tons per day. The capaci-
ty of the five waterworks in hte urban area is 66,500 tons per day. The pollution causeed
by factories and the pollution of Xiaoling River once had a severe effect on three of the
five waterworks that draw water from the Xiaoling River. The pollution is of seasonal
nature. It mnakes the already poor water supply even worse in the urban area of Jinzhou.
Due to the requirement for industrial development and population growth in the urban
area and especially in the development zones, the need for water supply will increase
greatly. Water supply has become the governing factor for development. Water shortage
12



is predicted to be 100,000 tons per day in 1995 and 200,000 tons per day in 2,000.
Since Xiaoling River and ground water are polluted and the river does not have enough
water for supply to a new waterworks, it is out of the question to build a large water-
works by the side of Xiaoling River. According to the "Report on the study of a Model of
Groundwater in Sectors of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers" approved by the Comnittee of
Geological Mineral Depots Reserves of Liaoning Province, there are rich and good quality
groundwater resources in the alluvial sectors of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers 15 to 25 km
away from the urban area. Of the extractable capacity of 1. 36 nillion rns/d, 200, 000
m3/d can be extracted in addition to the volume being used. The present water works pro-
ject is aimed at daily extraction of 100,000 ms, to fill in the gap caused by the polluted
water sources.
5. 1. 2 Nature of the Project for Curbing the Pollution Caused by Sewage from Jincheng
Paper Mill
This paper mnill polution control project includes projects for using pulp to make ad-
hesives, recovering paper making white water and reprocessing reed dust to make artificial
carbon.
The main puspose of the project is to reduce the pollution load on the lower reaches
of Daling River, and protect groundwater resources in the sectors between Daling and Xi-
aoling Rivers.
The groundwater in sectors between Daling and Xiaoling Rivers is now not only the
water supply base for Jinzhou, but also an important water supply for Jinxi and Panjin.
The quality of water has a close bearing on the health of the people and the development
of the economy of Jinzhou,Jinxi and Panjin. The industrial sewage from Jincheng Paper
Mill flows in the ditch on the east bank of Daling River and meets Daling River at Sanhe
village. In sections beyond Zhaojiawobo, Daling River supplies water horizontally to
groundwater layers. Downwards from Zhaojiawobo Daling supplies groundwater layers
vertically by percolation. In normal cases, sewage from the paper mill goes to groundwa-
ter layers through the sewage ditches by means of free infiltration. W9hen there is a signif-
icant flood in the water abundance period, the meeting point of the sewage ditch and Dal-
ing River is moved upwards to the section beyond Zhaojiawobo, and the sewage of the pa-
per mill flows into Daling River, which mnay go to water layers horizontally.
recycled paper                      13 e3obr *nd ""shmen



Jincheng Paper Mill is the main source of pollution for Daling River. The mill pro-
duces more than 95 Yo of the pollution load discharged into Daling Rever. In the Xibaqian
section of the lower reaches of the polluted Daling River the maximum COD content
reached 273 mg/l in 1991. Severe damages have been caused to the river ecology and the
maritime environment.
The above-mentioned facts show that the control of the pollution caused by Jincheng
Paper will is a key project for protecting the groundwater resources of Daling and Xiaol-
ing Rivers, improving water quality of Daling River and protecting the maritire environ-
ment off thie estuary of Daling River.

5.2.3.3  Noise
The pump house and the boiler facilities are major noise sources. In order to reduce noise, a
shock-danping cusion will be installed in the foundation of the pumps, telescopic shock-damping con-
nectors will be fitted to both the inlet and the outlet of the pumps and noise-absorbing windows and
doors will be fitted in the watch room.
Round the various pump houses in the pressure station, the water distribution works and other fa-
cilities, trees and grass will be planted to absorb noise and beautify the environment.

5. 3. 2. 2 Energy Consumption for the Project to Curb Water Pollution Cused by
Jincheng Paper Mill
This project requires additional electric power of 1083. 1 kwh/h. The present elec-
tric load of the paper mill is 14795. 2 kwh/h and the total power required in the future
will be 15878. 7 kwh/h. The thermo power plant in the mill now has the capability to
supply to a load of 19,899 kwh/h and there will be enough power and to spare for this
project
Thi project needs additional quantity of steam of 19 t/h, and the present steam con-
sumption in the mill is 122 t/h in winter, totalling 141 t/h in the future. But the present
power plant in the mill produces 259 t/h of steam, which is much more than enough for
future requirement. In sum, the project does not require any additional energy producing
facilities to set up.

5. 3. 3. 1 Technologies for curbing water pollution and the results
The targets of this project include:( 1) Recovery of thick red solution and production
of 150,000 tons of adhesive per year. (2) Daily purification of 30,000 tons of white
water from paper making, yearly recovery of 4,600 tons of fiber and 8,000 tons of tal-
cum; (3) Recovery of reed dust and yearly production of 4, 000 tons of artificially made
carbon.

See Fig. 5- 2 for the process of curbing sewage from pulp making.  Dulp is diwsharged-
in jet at full pressure from the steam boiler into the store container. Waste gas heats the
water for drainingby passing through the exchanger. Pulp is -umped from the store con-
tainer to the deslagger where heavy matterA such as metal are removed, then,passing the      < -S
intermediate pulp reservoir, goes to Section 1 double net draine.In this place the pulp's
concentration is increased from 3. 5%4 at the inlet to 2534 at the outlet. Solids and resid-
ual acids are removed from the pulp to become what is called thicred sluion, part of
which is sent back to the store container to dilute the pulp and balance of wiiich is sent to
the evaporating station to be condensed as adhesive. The pulp from the Section 1 double-
net drainer goes on to the Section 2 double-net drainer and after draining the pulp is sent
to a screen, and the thin red solution is sent to the store container while the surplus in dis-
charged into the sewage pipe.
By using the above-mentioned proces, the residual acids ante of the drained pulp
is reduced from 4, 000 ppm in the store container to 65 ppm. The total recovery ratio of
solids is 69. 28%. 3034 of the solids, however, will not be recovered. This is maily
recycled paper                   25                     efo" anid evrnnwrn



due to the limited demands of tLe market for adhesives. With the increase of the demand,
the recovery ratio of solids in the thick red solution shall be raised to over 95%, which
will be the target of the second phase project.
Adhesive Production line
The solids becomes adhesive when the sulfite pulp red solution containing 10. 4% of
solids condenses into a solution containing 50 to 51% of solids. To produce 150,000 tors
of adhesive per year requires to evaporate 1734.18 tons of water per day (72. 25 t/h).
If a simple evaporating facility is used to turn such a huge amount of water into vapor,
the amount of energy needed would be surprisingly high. The forced circulation, long
tubular or planar cavity multi-function evaporator now in use in China produces severe
scaling during the evaporating proces by heat. The main content of the scale is magne-
sium sulfate, which is not soluble in acid or alkali . hence very difficult to get rid of, re-
ducing the efficiency of evaporating process and increasing energy consumption.
For this project, the paper mill is going to use a horizontal jet film, vacuum evapo-
rator manufactured by AQVA-CHEN company in the US. The evaporator is being used
by six factories,which make sulfite pulp. In 1989 the Guangzhou Paper Mill bought a
400m2 jet film vacuum evaporator that evaporates 37. 3 tons of water per hour and pro-
duces one tone of vapor for every 4. 25 tons of water evaporated. Besides the advantages
of the average falling-film evaporator, this facility contains the thick red solution outside
the pipe while passing the vapor inside the pipe and features a powerful jet that prevents
scaing and mnakes it easy to clean the equipment.
It is planned to use a row of five-section, four-function evaporators with an effec-
tive area of 800m2 and an total area of 4, 000m2. One of the functions is cyclic
cleaning.
The type of evaporator will be finalized after an investption is made abroad.
Specification of the adhesive:
Specific weight: 1. 27/20C, pH6-7, solid content: 51%
Sulphonic acid: 8. 98%, CaO<0. 5%, MgO 4-5%
Sulphur<4 %
The evaporator station needs a floor area of 1. 500m2.

4,600 tons of fiber and 800 tons of talcum can be recovered.
At present there are four paper making workshops: No. 1, 2, 3 workshops make
printing paper and No. 4 workshop makes white decoration paper. See the table below for
dischargcd amount of white water.
The SS in the white water from the paper making workshops mainly coritains fiber
and talcum filler. The daily loss of fiber is measured to be 13. 52 t, and the yearly loss is
up to 4,600 tons, approximately 4. 5%o.
The real consumption of talcum filler is shown in the following table.
Each year 8000. 2 tons of talcum are lost with the discharged sewage.
The following method is used to treat the white water from paper making.
In the past multi-disk, double-drum, air-suspension and slant plate recoverers were
often used to recover pulp fiber from the white water, but these methods all failed to puri-
fy the white water, letting 70%Y of SS in white water go with sewage.
See Fig. 5-3 for white water treatment flow.
For this project, it is planned to use a homo-directional slant plate settling tank
patent desinged by Changsha Design Institute of the Ministry of Light Industry. The e-
quipment under consideration features slant plate reversal current which does not block
the pulp and the capability of water purification to 0 to 30ppzn. The flow chart of the
process is shown in Fig. 5- 3
The white water from the papernaking workshops flow into the catching tank, and
then is pumped to the purifier-separator, from which it flows to the static mixer. After
being mixed with 3/10000 Alum solution, the water goes to the presettling vessel,
where, blocked by the stabilizing plate, the regulating box and the-regulating wall, white
water allows part of its fiber and talcum to slowly settle to the pulp exit funnel. After this
primary settling process, the white water passes the settling tank and flows to the slant
plate settler for further settling. NVater is used regularly to wash the slant plate to prevent
pulp blocking the flow channel. Pulp and talcum are settled again to the pulp exit funnel
and the purified water overflows from the top and is sent through the recycling pipe back
to the pulp workshop for further use. Pulp material and talcum are sent back to paper-
making workshops for redistribution or to be filtered by the belt drainer into pulp cakes
with concentrations of 25 % and upwards, which can be sold to other paper mills.

Discharge amount of dust-laden reed chips
Thie production of each ton of pulp requires 2. 257 tons of reed. 6 %/0 of reed is lDst
in cutting and screening. The total amount of reed chips is 101 ,320X 2. 257X 6V' =
13.720 t/a, which contains 7. 69%  water, and 15. 48%  dust, and has a unit volume
weight of 81. 25kg/M3 (free piled).
Output of artificial Charcoal
It is found from tests that one ton of Charcoal can be produced for every 3. 5 tons of
reed chips. Yearly output of artificial Charcoal is 4,000 tons.
Method of production
At prcsent all the rced chips are dumped into the Daling River and the SS in the reed
chips constitutes 32. 4 i;; of the total. Therefore, it is imperative to reprocess these reed
chips if SS content in the sewage is to be reduced.
Reed chips from the round screen and dust separater are colected and then transport-
ed to the material barn, from which they are distributed to the spiral extruder-former.
The extruder-former press the reed chips into the form of bars, which are sent to carbide
furnaces. After 5 to 7 hours the temperature in the furnace rises to 360 to 400 deg c; and
reed chips are being carbonized at this temperature for 4 to 6 hours and then become arti-
ficial Carbon. See lFig. 5-4.

Element analysis
Carbon 66.74%, Hlydrogen 2. 911%,NitrogenO. 8_ o, Sulfur 0.68%.
Artificial Charcoal material balance
The combustible constitucnt is mainlv tar, which, according to the plan, will be
minxed with heavy oil and burnt together.

5. 3. 5  AnmtItv  to the Project for Curbing Water Pbf   . .fmd   11
Besides the project mentioned above, there are several alternative projects which are
technically feasible in controlling the water pollution caused by Jincheng Paper Mill.
5. 3. 5.1  Renovation off            _ii1
In developed countries most paper mills have replaced acid pulping with sulphate
pulping, which features a great advantage o; easiness in recovering waste solution to al-
most 95Y%. However, additional facilities are required for extraction, evaporation, com-
bustion, dust collection, and multi bleaching. To renovate an acid pulping paper mil inma
a sulphate pulping paper mill requires almost the same amount of funds as needed by the
construction of a brand new paper mill. So this alternative is prohibitively expensive.
5. 3. 5.2                  t          __

The operating cost for this alternative is found through calculation to be 2 4. 7 million
yuan/year. Considering the present status of China and the economic capability of
Jincheng Paper Mil:, this alternative requires large quantities of funds for capital con-
struction and a high operation cost and therefore it is unaffordable.
5. 3. S. 3 Blocking the sewage flow
In order to protect the groundwater in the sector area of Daling and Xiaoling rivers
in the lower reaches to Jincheng Paper Mill, sewage from the mill may be blocked and di-
verted to the river reaches 35 km downward from the paper mill by using civersion pipes
of 1. 0 m in diameter. This alternative would require an investment of 35 mil!ion
yuan.
Although this alternative can protect the groundwater in the sector area, it fails to
reduce the poUution load on the lower reaches of Daling River and the coastal waters.
From the pointview of ecology protection for the river and the sea, it is not a good alter-
native because, in addition of failing to protect the overall water environment. it involves
quite a large quantitv of funds.
After the above analysis of alternat,ives, it is concluded that the first mnentioned pro-
ject is the most feasible both economically and technically for controlling water pollution
caused by Jincheng Paper Mill.
6 EIA FOR THE ENVIRONMENT OF DALING RIVER
6. 1 Scope of Assessmcnt
The new waterworks of Jinzhou is located on the right hand side bank of Daling River be-
tween Liuduan and Zhutuozi. Daling River has no direct hydraulic relation to the ground-
water in this area, but its water quality can still threaten the water quality of water
sources.
34t
recycled paper                    31ologv and envranni



ETis EIA relates to the present status of water of Dating River between Zhangji3bao
and the estuary of Daling to the sea, covering a distance of 80 km.
6. 2 Standards and Factors for Assessment
The assessment of the present status of river water is made in accordance with Stan-
dard GB3838-88 Category V.
Based on the pollutant discharge along Daling River, pollution for four kinds of pol-
lutants are selected for EIA, namely, COD, SS, oils and volatile phenol.
6. 3 Present Status of Pollution of Daling River and Its Assessment
6. 3. 1 Miethod of Assessment
The assessment method involves the use of the findings from regular surveys and
measures conducted by the Environment Survey Station of Jinzhou at the two sections at
Zhangjiabao and Xibaqian betveen 1983 and 1991, and the pollution indices for the dry
season, full water season and medium water level season. lbe following equation is
used:
C.
C..
Where:- I    pollution index of a certain pollutant
C- measured value of that pollutant (mg/I)
C,- standard limit of that pollutant (mg/1)
6. 3. 2 E:A Findings
Findings of status survey and assessment are contained in Tables 6-1( atiuto 6-6.
From these tables it can be seen that:
(1 ) The pass percent of oils in the river was 98%. In the dry season in 1990. only
in the Zhangjiabao section did the measured value surpass the limit by a factor of 0. 15.
Mhis is because the radial flow of the river in that season was extremely small.
(2) The pass percent of volatile phenol was 98%. Only in the medium water level
season in 1983 in the Xib3qian section did the measured value exceed the limit by a factor
35



of 0. 84.
(3) For COD, the situation was verv severe. It was not uncommon that the mea-
sured values exceeded the limit several times or even several dozens of times. COD, is the
worst for aU its values surpassed the limit. The out of bound ratio of CODMvalues was
88. 4 5/% in Zhangjiabao section and 100% in Xibaqian section, which was higher than
that mesured at Zhangjiabao. This was caused by the discharge of sewage into river by
Jincheng Paper Mill.
(4) The measured SS values were extremely high, the content of SS was found be-
tween 179 and 37,932 mg/l. As little ground is covered with vegetation and much water
and soil are washed away in the reaches of Daling river, the river contains large quanti-
ties of sand, which decrease from fuU water season to mnedium water level season to dry
season.
The COD value of Daling River exceeds significantly the limit set by the standard for
the quality of Category V water and this is closely related to the high content of SS in the
water. The Environment Protection Science Research Institute of Jinzhou has made a spe-
cial study of the interrelation between COD and SS of Daling River, which has proved
that the 95% COD and the 70%D COD,bare both absorbed in SS. Therefore. a supple-
mentary assessment was made of the soluble COD value after removal of SS absorption
and the results are shown in Tables 6-7 and 6-8. From the tabled results one can see that
after deduction of SS absorption, the COD=  value was still well beyond th. limit. The
out-of-bound ratio was 17% in Zhangjiabao and 31 % in Xibaqian. However, after de-
duction of SS absorption, the COD. value dropped significantly and according to the EIA
there were two limit surpassings in Zhangjiabao in full water season, one limit crossing
respectively in full water season and medium water level season, two crossings in dry sea-
son in Xibaqiaon section. All these crossings were within a factor of 1.
The high content of SS in Daling River is caused by the severe loss of water and soil
in the upper reaches. The washed-away water and soil carry large quantity of organic
natters into the Daling River. This is the main cause for the severe COD pollution at
2hangjiabao in the upper reaches section of Jincheng during the full water season.

6. 4. 1 Prediction Model for Water Quality of Daling Rlver
Daling River runs transversely across the west part of Liaoning province. Much wa-
ter and soil are washed away into the river in the upper reaches of Daling. In rainy sea-
son the water in the river rises frantically, and carries large quantities of sand. According
to the information obtained by observation and messurement, the average annual sand
content in the river has exceeded 1 Okg/mr in the past years, ranking first in China's sandy
river. Therefore, in setting up a model for water quality assessment and in considering
the general law governing river pollution, focus is laid on the impact of mud and sand on
water quality.
According to the mass conservation law, the following basic equation is
established:
a c    ac    ac '    aRIl _i an2   I                   (6-1)
a i    z    a,    a       ag i      7T7
Where: C- concentration of pollutant En river water
V- average current velocity in the cross section of the river
M- discreet coefficient
B,- concentration of suspended mobile mud and sand
02-conccntration of pushed mobile mud and sand
R- hydraulic radit;s of river cross section
n,-concentration of oollutant obsorbed on the surface of pushed mobile mud
and sand
n2-  concentration of pollutant absorbed on the surface of settled mobile mud
and sand
n3-concentration of pollutant absorbed on the surface of mud grains on the
river bed
Based on the actual conditions. the following assumptions are made regarding the
above equation:
a. The quantity of pushed mobile mud and sand is far less than that of suspended
mobile mud and sand, hence- i, =Oz
45



b. The quantitv of a pollutant absorbed by river bed mud is in direct proportion to
that by suspended mud and sand, that is, n3=b3n,
c. The quantity of a pollutant absorbed by suspended mobile mud and sand is in di-
rect proportion to the concentration of that pollutant as resolved in the river, that
is, nl=b,c
Thus, the above equation can be transformed into the following:
a .  _=, a c + A a 2c                    6
where:  = 1 + O1b1 +   bA
Since both the new waterworks facilities and the Jincheng Paper Mill are located in
the rnid and lower reaches of the Daling River, where the river is wide and shallow and
suffers from a great number of pollution sources, the above equation is solved numnerical-
ly by implicit differential method. The detailed proces of solution are skipped in this re-
port because there is not enough space in here.
The block diagram of calculation is shown in Fig. 6-1.
The implicit differential proceeds as follows: discrelize equation (2) and the follow-
ing matrix is obtained:

6. 4. 2 Determination of Basic Paramrneers of the Predictdon Model
6. 4. 2. 1 Flow rate
Daling River has characteristics typical of rivers in north China. The change of sea-
sons has a significant impact on the flow of the river. Flow varies much over different
seasons of the year. Statistics of river flow are nade for different seasons for the Daling
Rivcr by the Hydrology Station of Jinxian County. The data supplied by Jinxian Hcydrol-
ogy Station are shown in Table 6-9.
Avcrage Flow in Different Hydrological Years  Table 6-9

County 500 rnetcrs in the lower reaches to Jinxian yIvdrology Station (upper rzaches to
the sewage discharge outlet of Jincheng Paper Mill). Water is channelled to the irrigation
network of Jinxian between mid April and mid September every year. The average quan-
tity of channelled water is 64. 4 million tons per vear, i. e. . 4. 87r1n/s. During the early
months of water drawing the quantity of channeled water is relatively greater than in the

completion of the project for controlling the pollution caused by Jincheng Paper Mill,
At present, Jincheng Paper Mill discharges large quantities of sewage and pollutants.
The results of water quality simulation using the model described in § 6. 4. 1 indicate a
high level of pollution in Daling River (See Tables 6-15,6-16). 'The highest COD
concentration in dry season is 117. 3 mg/h. This is because in dry season the flow of Dal-
ing River drops sharply while the discharge of sewage by Jincheng Paper Mill is in large
quanity. In full water season, mud and sand and suspended matters increase in quantity
-due to powerful washing by the river, and therefore the background value of COD be-
comes sLightly larger tan of the medium water level season. The simulated value of COD
in full water season is 76. 7mg/l, the highest of all seasons, and the value of medium
water level season is 50. 4mg/l.
After the completion of the project for renovating the paper mill, the yearly dis-
charge of sewage from the paper mill is 12. 113 million tons, only 51% of the pre-pro-
,ect period; the total COD is 20,637 t/a, 32% of pre-project value. From the prediction
one can see that both sewage and pollutant discharge will drop sharply and the pollution of
water in Daling River will decrease significantly. The -prediction indicates that in dry sea-
son the maximum COD is 60. 9mg/l, 48% lower than the present value. Thit shows the
great benefit the control project will bring. The highest concentration in full water season
is 39. 8mg/i, also 48% lower than the pre-project value. As there is less water in the
river in nedium water level season than in fiu water season, the diluting capability of the
river in the medium season is relatively weak and the concentration of suspended matters
and pollutants is relatively higher. The highest COD value is therefore 48. 0mg/I, 4. 8%
lower than the pre-project value.
6. 4. 3. 2 Analysis of the Prediction of Soluble CODw4 for Daling River
When the river is supplying water to the underground layers of earth, the soluble
components in the water (including soluble components separated from suspended matters)
may enter water-containing layers by permeation, but mxst of the elements carried by
suspended matters cannot permeate into the water-containing layers From the viewpoint
of groundwater supply, the soluble components of COD%b in the water of Daling River
can affect the quality of groundwater by permeation while the non-soluble CODum carried
by suspended matters has almost no effect on the quality of groundwater. Therefore, the
prediction of the pollution by soluble COD# before and after the completion of the pollu-
55



tion control project for Jincheng Paper Mill and the project of constructing a new water-
works is of great importance for protecting the groundwater resources in the sectors of
Daling and Xiaoling Rivers.
Table 6-14 to 6-16 give the simulation results for total CODM,at cross sections in
the lower reaches to the meeting point of Daling River and the sewage ditch of Jincheng
Paper Mill as well as the simulation results for soluble COD1and non-soluble CODn.
Simulation findings show that in the dry season of a medium water level year the
highest soluble CODun. content in the water in cross sections in the lower reaches of D.i.ng
River will drop from 36. 4mg/l before the completion of the two projects to 18. 9mg/l af-
ter the completion of the two projects, when the water quality of Daling River will im-
prove greatly in the dry season thanks to the positive effects.brought about by the pollu-
tion control project for Jincheng Paper Mill. After the completion of the new water.
works, the flow rate of the river in its lower reaches will decrease on account of the in-
creased water supply to groundwater layers, thus adversely affecting the water quality of
the river. However, this adverse effect is much smaller than the positive effect mentioned
above.
In the medium water season of a medium water year, the highest soluble COD>,,, val-
ue drops from 15. 8mg/l before the two projects to 14. 9mg/l after the completion of the
two projects. There is a decrease of 5. 7 /o. In full water season in medium water year,
after the completion of the two projects, the highest soluble CODu content in the lower
reach cross sections of Dating will be 12. 3mg/l, 48. 3%a lower than the highest. content
23. 8mg/l before the completion of the two projects.
In sum, the completion of the two projects will greatly improve the water quality of
Daling River.
6. .1. *l Stramegy of Preventing and Controlling Water Polution of Daling River
The prevention and control of water pollution of Daling Rive. should include the
preservation of the specific functions of each section of the river and protective measures
should be taken in an appropriate nmanner with regard to the different functions of Lhe riv-
er sections: the main target is to protect and improve the water quality of Dling River and
the groundwater resources. Regional planning should bt combined with planning based on
river reachle.s protection of eco,lngical environment with control of pollution. environ-
recycled paDer                      56                    ecoeg'v and enmimumenn



ment protection projects with scientific research and moritoring, and near term planning
with long term programmer, thus protecting the water quality of Daling River and the en-
vironinent surrounding it.
In the upper reaches of Daling River, work should be focused on the preservation of
ecology and the prevention of loss of water and soil while the control of pollution sources
should be enhanced. The background value of pollutants in the lower reaches of Daling
River, CODm, for example, is relatively high because the river contains large quantity of
rmd and sand which have high capability of absorbing poUutant. This is an important
feature regarding the change in water quality of Daling River. The control of mud and
sand in Daling River is art important part of the project to control the water pollution of
Daling River.
In the lower reaches of Daling River, focus should be on the prevention and control
of industrial pollution. In this area, sources of pollution are located at Jincheng Town
and Dalinghe Town. The Jincheng Paper Mill in Jincheng Town is the principal pollution
source for the Daling River. The sewage discharge from that paper mill constitutes 70 %
of the total from Jinzhou. In ternm of pollutants (COD) discharged , the paper mill pro-
duced 97. 1% of the total of the city. Therefore, the most iperative target in control-
ling the pollution of Daling River is to control the sewage discharge from Jincheng Paper
MM.
The above analysis indictes that the strategy of preventing and controlling the water
pollution of Daling River should take into account both the preservation of ecology and
the control of pollution sources. Based on the specific conditions in the Jinzhou reaches of
Daling River, plans for pre-venting and controlling water pollution shall be implemented
in three phases, near term, mid term and long term.
Near term1 This is the first project for controlling water pollution caused by
Jincheng Paper Mill The project starts with the renovation of the pulping technology, in-
volves the use of the red pulping water to make adhesive, the recovery of white water and
the use of reed chips to make artificial Charcoal. After the completion of this project, the
paper mill will reduce its discharge of COD, by 44.987 tons, suspended matters by
34,422 t-, and sewage by 30, 000m, enabling the city to reduce its discharge of COD into
Daling River by 66. 5% and sewage by 31. 2%. This project plays an important role in
improving the water quality of Daling River, protecting the new waterworks at Liuduan
57



and improve the quality of the coastal waters. It will brlng huge benefits to the environ-
mnent. Tbe project is scheduled to complete by the end of 1994 and the total fund required
for capital construction is 56. 55 million yuan.
Mid term: This is the second project for controlling water pollution cused by
Jincheng Paper Mill. The targets of the project Include the continuation of recovering the
red water for comprehensive use and the construction of a bio-chemical sewage treatnent
station at the paper mill. After the completion of this project, the discharge of sewage
from the mill wiil be up to the standards. The total fund required for the project is 40
million yuan.
In addition, sewage control projects will also be implernented for Jinxian Paper Mill
and Jwnxian Chemical Fertilizer Factory. The objective is that the sewage from these two
places shall be tread up to standards before it is discharged. The fund needed by the pro-
jet is 15 million yuan.
In addition, sewage control projects will also be implemented for Jinxian Paper ;1ill
and Jinxian Chemical Fertilizer Factory. The objective is that the sewage from these two
places shall be treated up to standards before it is discharged. The fund needed by the pro-
ject is 15 million yuan.
After the cornpletion of these mid-term projects, the discharge of COD into Daling
River will be reduced by 17,300 t/a, and the discharge of COD from the entire city will
be down 92. 1%.
Long-term project: This is the Dalinghe Town Sewage Treatment Station project.
Tte station is rated as Class I station which is able to treat 60,000m2/d of sewage. The
project involves an investment of 20 million yuan.
Water and earth conservation project for Daling River reaches: In order to th.or-
oughly improve the water quality of Daling River, it is necesary to carry out the project
for conservation of water and earth at roaling River reaches, which aius at reducing the
amount of soil and sand washed away by the river and the organic matters carried with
the soil and sand. The project for water and soil conservation at the Daling River reaches
will have to be organized by the relevant local governments and coordinated by authorities
at higher levels. Water and soil conservation is a long-term task requiring a lot of persis-
tance. Tne whole project needs a fund of about 600 million yuan.

7 ASSESSMENT OF UNDERGROUND WATER ENVIRONMENT
7. 1 Scope of Assessment
Scope of Assessment of underground water includes the valley plain of Daling River
and Nuer River in the urban district of linzhou City with an area of lOlkrn2 and the fresh
water zone in the niddle and upper part of the Daling and Xiaollng Rivers fan limited in
the front edge by the salt water boundary where the water source is located, covering an
area of 911k1n2. The hills and valleys outside this area the salt water distribution area in
the front edge of the river fan are not assessed.
7. 2 Assessment of Present Status of Underground Water Environment
7. 2. 1 Status of Underground Water Resources
7. 2. 1. 1 Underground water reserves and its changing conditions
7. 2. 1. 1. 1 Underground water in Xiaoling River Valley
Underground water in the urban district of Jinzhou City is mainly stored in the val-
ley flat and stream terrace on the banks of the Xiaoling River and Daught River, cover-
ing an area of I Olkm2. The water-bearing stratum is mainly a gritstone formation with a
thickness of 4-12m. Above it is sandy clay and sandy soil with a thickness of 2-3m
and below it is base rock. Underground water is stored at a depth of 4-8m. Water Sup-
ply of a single well is normally 1. 000-3, ,OOOm/d. Water-bearing stratums in the hill,
valley and slope area are thin and unstable, containing very small amount of water. Wa-
ter supply of a single well ir. this area is less than 500'-100m/d. having no value for
providing central water supply.-
Underground water is replenished mainly by seeping rain water and river water and
also by underground water runoff from upper river valley. Seeping irrigation water and
city sewage water provide little replenishment. Underground water in this area is mainly
extracted by nanual recovery with a small amount flowing out in the form of under-
ground water runoff.
59



7. 2. 1. 1. 2 Underground water in Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan
This area can be dividud into two subareas according to different underground water
storage conditions and hydraulic nature:
Ground water-bearing area: It is located at the top of the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers
fan and the whole Xiaoling River fan, covering an area of 400km. Te water-bearing
stratum is made up of gritstones deposited in the early and midddle Pleistocene with a thick-
ness of 30-60m, increasing gradually from northwest to southeast. It is covered at the
top by sandy clay and silty sandy soil formation with a thickness of 3-1Om. The aque-
ous stratum in the river valley flat is directly exposed. The aqueous stratum has a good
water permeability. Water supply of a single well is normally 3,000-10D,000m3/d and
reaches 10, 000-20, 000m3/d at maximum. Underground water is stored at a depth of 3
-8m.
Double-layer water-bearing area: It is located in the middle of the Daling River
fan, covering an area of 410km2 and containing a shadow and a deep aqueous stratum.
'The shadow aqueous stratum is composed of deposited gritslones of the early Pleistooene
and has a thickness of 20-40m, the top plate of the water separation s;tatum being lo-
catod at a depth of 10'-20m. Water supply of a singlet well is 5,000-10O,OOOms/d.
The deep aqueous stratum is made up of gritstones of the middle and late Pleistocene and
has a thickness of 20-60m. The top plate of the water separation stratum is located at a
depth of 50-80m and made up of clay of thc middle Pleistocene with a thickness of a-
15m. Water supply of a single well from this stratum is 1. 000-5.  OOOm/d. The shad-
ow and deep stratums have a similar water head and water depth is normally 3--5m.
The new water supplies project is located between Liuduan and 7hutuo, in the tran-
sitional zone of ground water and double-layer water. The hydrogeological structure is
shown in Fig 7-1.
7. 2. 1. 2 Underground water\ supply resource
Underground water suppply resource is calculated by adding amounts of various sup-
plies based on balanced verification of water supplies. Tbe amounts of the following water
supplies in typical years ae calculated respectively: penetrated rain water supply, pene-
trated river water supply, penetrated irrigation water supply, penetrated sewage water
supply and undeground water current supply. The supply resource is represented by the
total amount of various supplies.

7. 2. 1. 2. 1 Calculation of penetrated rain water quantity
It is calculated by using the penetrated rain water supply factor and the following
formula:
QPmwi4r "=e - a EPF
WYhere rainfall(P) in typical years is calculated using a series of data in 1934-1979
taken from Suface Water Resources in Liaoning Province published in 1984 by Hydrolog-
ical Station of Liaoning Province. According to the data obtained from core analysis,
penetrated rain water supply factor (a) is as follows:
Sandy clay   0.14-0.19
Sandy soil  0. 20-0. 25
Silty sand   0. 28-0. 34
Gritstone   0. 35-0. 38
7. 2. 1. 2. 2 Calculation of penetrated river water quantity
It is calculated with the differential flow of the upper and lower sections using hy-
drological data and measured current data obtained in many years or with Darcy's flow
law.
7. 2. 1. 2. 3 Calculation of penetrated irrigation water quantity
It is calculated using agricultural. irrigation data and the following formula:

7. 2. 1. 2. 5 Calculation of penetrated sewage water quantity
It is calculated using annual amount of sewage discliarge and a penetration factor

7. 2. 1. 3 Underground water recovery resource
Underground water recovery resource is calculated and assessed on the principle that
suplus supply will make up for short supply and advantage of the regulating capability of
the water-bearing stratum will be taken.
The average thickness of the aqueous stratum in the Xiaoling River Valley plain is
small, only 7. 85m. The storage resource is 158,570, OOOM3 when it is calculated with a
supply factor of 0. 20.. As the aqueous stratum has a small regulating capacity and most
of the present water sources recover underground water on a continuous basis, the
amount of supply is less than the amount of recovery in dry years. To ensure normal re-
covery, water stored in the aqueous stratum will be extracted, thus causing drop in water
level. When calualtion is made on the basis of three successive dry years, to keep dynam-
ic water levcl of extraction wells within the rnax. permissible drop, it is desirable to take
average underground water supply resource as the recovery resource, i. e, the recovery
resource would be 56,600,000m3/a (155,000ms/d).
The underground water recovery resource in the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan is
calculated by using an established mathematical model of water quantity. The recovery

7. 2. 2. 2  Area which exceeds standard in single item.
It is located between the middle and front edge of the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers
fan, in the area where Xinzhuangzi. Jianye and Yanjia village are situated. It contains di-
carbonate-type fresh water with a mineralization less than 1 g/l. Water quality basically
meets quality standard for drinking water except for Fe content which is normally 0. 5-
3mg/I, exceeding standard 1 -10 times. Maximum Fe content can reach 6 mg/l.
7. 2. 2. 3 Area which exceeds standard in two or more itemrs
It is located in XiaoLing River valley and the front edge of Dating and Xiaoling
Rivers fan, including the area where Jianyie, Dayou, Baqian are situated and the area a-
long the Xiaoling River banks. It contains dicarbonate fresh water with a Fe and F con-
tent exceeding the standard. F content is 2-6 mg/1I exceeding the standard 1-5 times.
Underground water in Xiaoling River vaUcy is seriously polluted. Petrol content along the
river generally exceeds the standard. It is rnore than 0. 05mg/i and in some parts as high
as 0. 6-0. 9mg/I. In some sections near the river, COD,.4and SO 2content exceeds the
standard, CODm,. content being 4-Smg/l and SO?4 content 250-450mg/l.

According to the environmental problems that appear after completion of the water

lows 2
7. 3. 1. 1 As the underground water quantity model (finite difference value simulation)
for the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan is set up for estimation of ten average years (P=
50%) and three semi-dry years (p = 80%), the estiration of impact of Daling River
Water on the water quality of the Liuduan Water Source is also for a period of 13
years.
7. 3. 1. 2 For the estimation of impact on water quality of the Liuduan Water Source,
based on the actual data, each as the pollution factors obtained from analysis of the Dal-
ing River water and the degree of non-compliance of single factor content, COD and
CjHsOH are selected as the estimated factors of water quality of the Liuduan Water
Source.
7. 3. 1. 3 According to the equilibrium domain of node No. 317, the supply quantity of
Boundary 1 (ground-water area) and the initial concentration of the estimated factors in
the Liuduan Water Source section obtained when the underground water quatity model for
the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan is set up, the supply quantity in Boundary I (node
No. 317) and the coucentiation of the estimated factors (to be calculated), estimation is
Tade with linear relationship.
7. 3. 1. 4 When estimating impact on water quality of the Liuduan Water Source, water
quality in mediumyear (P=50%) and semi-dry year (P=80%) is estimated according
to the water quality in dry, full water and medium water seasons.
7. 3. 1. 5   Eetiration and assesswent should be made of impact on existing water
sources, suction well failure area and ecological environrment.
7. 3. 1. 6 The area where Fe and F content in the underground water of Daling and Xi-
aoling Rivers fan exceeds standard is mrainly located to the south of the southern fan, out-
sid the impact of the Liuduan Water Source. As it has no impact on water- quality, it will
not be assessed.
7. 3. 1. 7 When the water quatity model for the Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan is set
up, the southern salt water-fresh water boundary is established with a positive slope.
Therefore .o environmental problens will be caused by penetration of sea water. This

stable valley being 0. 83 mg/I. All peaks (high concentration) appear in the medium
water seasons, ranging from 1. 13 to 1. 31 mg/I, stable peak being 0. 25 mg/l. Stable
COD concentration in dry seasons is 0. 103, ranging from 0. 93 to 1. 10 mg/I. COD
concentrations in the three seasons in 10th year (medium water year) are estimated to be
1. 03, 0. 83 and 1. 22 mg/l with an increase in concentration of 0. 53, 0. 36 and
0. 59 mg/l. Concentrations in 13th year (semi-dry year) are estimated to 1. 10, 0. 87
and 1.31 mg/I for the three seasons, with an increase in concentration of 0. 60, 0. 40
and 0. 68 mg/I respectively.
It can be seen from the shape of the estimated CJHsOH concentration curve that val-
leys and peaks also appear in full water season and medium water season respectively.
Valleys change from 0. 0018 to 0. 002 mg/I, stable valley being 0. 0019 mg/I. Peaks
are in the range of 0. 0023- 0. 0027 mg/I, stable peak being 0. 0025 mg/l Stable
CgHsOH concentration in the dry senson is 0. 0023 mgjI, changing from 0. 0020 to
0. 0024. As estimated in the medium water year, C.H.OH concentration in 10th year are
0. 0023, 0. 0019 and 0. 0025 mg/l respectively for the ftree seasons, with an increase
of 0. 0013, 0. 0009 and 0. 0012 mg/l. As estimated in the dry year, concentrations in
the three seasons in 13th year are 0. 0024, 0. 0020 and 0. 0027 with an increase of
0. 0013, 0. 001 and 0. 0014 mg/I respectively.
The water quaiity esmation results for the liuduan Water Source section show that
the estimated COD concentrations in the three seasons in mdiuum water years and semi-
dry years do not excoeed the standard, while the estimated C4HOH concentrations do not
exceod the standard in full water seasons, but slightly exceed the standard in dry and
medium water seaso  by 0. 0001-0. OD06 mg/l It is therefore concluded that the D31-
ing River water has little impact on the underground water quality.

tion of suction well failure areas only occurs in 3rd successive dry year (P=80%o). Wa-
ter level in the whole area wiU rise in full water year, reducing the failure area to that in
medium water year.
Whether the ecological environment will change in the suction well failure area is an
environmental problem of common concern. This question can be answered by actual in-
vestigation. Rainfall in 1989 was only 418 r-mm and suction well failure occurred in May
and June in WangiiawopuOXi nzhuangziULiuduan. Bozi, Yaotur and other villages. But no
trees or crops were found withered due to water level dropping to below 8 m. indicating
that the ecological environment in the suction well failure area is nornmal.

Jincheng Paper Mill on Underground Water
After the project of curbing water pollution caused by the Jincheng Paper Mill is
completed, the river water environment below Jincheng section will be improved. As the
escape caned will be flooded in full water season, the pollutants in the canel will affect
water quality of the Liuduan Water Source. So concentrations of COD and CjisOH in
underground water in full water seaon are predicted, while their concentration in the dry
and medium water season will remain unchanged.

7. 4 Determination and Protection of Water Source Protection Area
Liuduan Water Source protection area is deternined according to the area of depth
dropping field and the planned recovery of underground water in Liuduan at
10,000 r3m/d which is determined using water quantity model for the Daling and Xiaol-
ing Rivers fan (see Fig. 7-11 for details).
The protection area covers an area of 4. 9 km2. In this area, river section in Bound-
ary 1 is 1i,141 m long. Protection recommnendations are as follows:
7. 4. 1  Trees should be planted all over the water source protection area. No garbage or
poisonous materials are allowed to be stored there. ht is strictly prohibited to use
sewage water to irrigate farm land.
7. 4. 2   It is strictly prohibited to discharge sewage water to the river banks of Boundary
1 in the water source protection area. Existing pollution sources should be con-
trolled and sewage water should be discharged according to national discharge
standards.
7. 4. 3  ln the river section between the hills where Daling River panes to noed No.
316, sewage water should also be discharged according to national discharge
standards.
7. 4. 4  In the section where Liuduan Water Source is located, a dynamic underground

7. 5 Conclu3ions for the Assessment of Underground Water
From assessment of Xiaoling and Nuer River valley plain in the urban district of
Jinzhou City and underground water environment in Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan
where the water source will be built, we have drawn conclusions as follows:
7. 5. 1  Thbe assessed area has underground water resource of 515,000,000 m3/a,
57,000,000 m3/a in Xiaoling River valley and 458, 000, 000 m3/a in Daling
and Xiaoling Rivers fan. Underground water recovery resource amounts to
577, 000,000 m3/a,  of  which   489,000,000-   527,000,000 m'/a
(1,340,000-1,440,000 m3/d) in Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan, central
recovery  accounting for 840,000 m3'/d and distributed recovery  for
500,000-600,000 mJ/d.
7.5. 2  Underground water in Daling River fan and part of Xiaoling River fan is up to
the drinking water quality standard. Single-item non-compliance area is mainly
located in the middle and front edge of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers fan where Fe
content exceeds standard 1-10 times. Two-item non-compliance area is located
in Xiaoling River valley plain and the front edge of Daling and Xiaoling Rivers
fan where Fe and F- content exceeds standard 1-5 times. Underground water,
in Xiaoling River valley is seriously polluted, oil content along the river and
COD and SOW in part of the section near the river exceed standard. The above-
mentioned non-compliance areas are far from te downstream of underground
water flow to the suggested water source and therefore will not affect the water
source.
7. 5. 3  It can be seen from the prediction results of impact of river water on the water
quality of the water source that the impact of river water on the water quality of
the water source is small. Prediction results of underground water level dropping
in existing water sources show that little impact will be produced on existing wa-
ter sources.
recycled paper                    88                  Ch'isk~ ancd ernminnmru



7. 5. 4 Prediction results of depth dropping field extension in Liuduan Water Source
show that suction well failure area after three successive dry year wiU be larger
than that in medium water year, but it will reduce and restore to the medium
water year level after fuUl water year has come. No change in ecological envi-
ronment will take place in the suction well failure area.
7. 5. 5 The water source protection area Is determined according to the predicted results
of the water quantity model. It Is neesary to strengthen the water environmen-
tal protection work in the protected area, so as to ensure the nornul exploitation
of water sources

Bohai is a half-closed sea bay. Iiaodong Bay is situated in its north, the shores are
bounded by Jinxi, Jinzhou. Panjin, Yinkou and Dalian areas. Daling River enters into
Liaodong Bay somewhere near north latitude 45-52' ,east longitude 121-35' , the water
depth of the sea area near the river mouth is 2-4m, belonging to sea areas of a shallow
sea. The scope of this aessment is on the sea areas bounding the river mouth of Daling
River.

8. 5. 1 Prediction Method of Sea Area Environment
v}
The computation of Liaodoa Bay sea area tidal currents and polluting mattc  diffusion is
rade using the ADI (alternating direction implicit ) method established by J. J.
Leenaertse, to find the numerical solution of the continuity equation, momentum equa-
tion and diffusion equation of the sea area.
The genemal form of momentum equation and continuity equation for shallow sea
tidal current may be written as:

In the equation 8-1-8-4:
X, Y, Z-external force components acting on the unit mass of the system
u,V,W-  now speed components in X,Y,Z directions
P-pressure
p- density
T,- the projection on i-axis of the friction stress acting on a unit area on i-plane
(i. e. plane perpendicular to the i-axis)
In the computation the step-length of differential network is 100 m. step-length of
time is 480s. Since in Liaodong Bay the half-day tide is irregular, so it is treated as a
full-day tide. 24 hours make up a computation period. The computation is shown in

The diffusion equation is also solved using the ADI method, adopting the same alternating
network coordinate system as in the tidal current numerical value computation. For flow
speed and water level, the tidal current value and tidal positional value outputted from the
7-th computation period in the tidal current computation are used.
8. 5. 2 Prediction of Impact of the Project on Sea Area Environment
After the start of the pollution-water treatment project of Jincheng Paper Mill, the
quantity of COD into sea in full-water period from Daling River decreased to 221,866. 3
kg/d. Considering that the impact of Daling River in full and dry periods on seawater
quality is typical, so a diffusion numerical model is used to conduct the present state mod-
elling and prediction computation of seawater quality in full water and dry periods. The
comparison of water quality in sea area near the river mouth after the start of the
Jincheng Paper Mill pollution water treatment is shown in Table 8-4.
As seen from Table 8- 4, during the full water period and dry period, after the start
of the Jincheng Paper Mill pollution water treatment project, the water quality of sea area
near Daling River mouth is improved. The inprovement of water quality is more evident
during the fuU water period critical to seawater breeding.

9 ASSESSMENT AND IMPACT ANALYSIS OF THE PRESENT STA-
TUS OF THE ATMOSPHERIC AND NOISE ENVIRONMENT
9. 1 Assessment of the Present Status cf Atmospheric Environment and the
Impact Analysis
9. 1. 1 Scope of Assessment
The scope of assessment on atmospheric environment around Jincheng Paper Mill is
deterniined according to the 100 m high smoke funnel of the Mill's thermo-electric power
station, it is defined as an area 20 km around the center of the Mill. The scope of assess-
ment on atmospheric environment around tLh Water Source Project Pumping Station and
Water Distribution Plant is determined according to the boiler chimney height to be an
area centered at the chimney with a radius of 1. '. km.
9. 1. 2 Standard and Factors for Assessment
9. 1. 2. 1 Standard of assessment
The assessment of the present state and imnpact on atmospheric environment adopts
the Class I and Class  standard, respectively, of the GB309a-82 n Quality Standard
of Atmospheric Environment" according to the different functional areas.
9. 1. 2. 2 Assessment factor
For the assessment factor on the present state of atmospheric environment around
Jincheng Paper Mill the SO2, NO., T. S. P are selected.
For assessment of impact on atmospheric environment around Water Source Project
Pumping Station and the Water Distribation Plant SO2, NOQ, T. S. P are selected.
For assessment of impact on atmospheric environment of the Artificial Charcoal Pro-
ject H2S, CO are selected.
9. 1. 3 Assesmnt of the Present Status of Atmospheric Environment
For monitoring of the present state of atmospheric environment around Jincheng Pa-
per Mill 10 point positions are laid. The distribution of the point positions are shown in
Table 9-1 and Fig 9-1.
